25:T3af6,<entryFree id="n3222" key="بُلُوغٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">بُلُوغٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">بلوغ</orth>
                  </form> [inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغَ</foreign>] and <foreign lang="ar">إِبْلَاغٌ</foreign> [inf. n. of   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n3222-1" target="ابلغ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n3226"/></foreign>, but it seems that <foreign lang="ar">ابلاغ</foreign> is here a mistranscription for <foreign lang="ar">بَلَاغٌ</foreign>, which is, like <foreign lang="ar">بُلُوغٌ</foreign>, an inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغَ</foreign>, and this observation will be found to be confirmed by a statement immediately following this sentence,] signify The <hi rend="ital">reaching, attaining, arriving at,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">coming to, the utmost point of that to which,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">towards which, one tends</hi> or <hi rend="ital">repairs</hi> or <hi rend="ital">betakes himself, to which one directs his course,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">which one seeks, pursues, endeavours to reach, desires, intends,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">purposes; whether it be a place, or a time, or any affair or state or event that is meditated or intended or determined or appointed:</hi> and sometimes, the <hi rend="ital">being at the point thereof:</hi> so says Abu-1-Kásim in the Mufradát. (TA: [in which it is said, in the supplement to the present art., that <foreign lang="ar">بَلَاغٌ</foreign> signifies The <hi rend="ital">reaching, attaining, arriving at,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">coming to, a thing.</hi>]) You say, <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغَ المَكَانَ</foreign>, (S, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">المَنْزِلَ</foreign>, (Msb,) [aor.     
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar">بَلُغَ</orth>
                  </form>,] inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">بُلُوغٌ</foreign> (S, K) [and <foreign lang="ar">بَلَاغٌ</foreign>, as shown above], <hi rend="ital">He reached, attained, arrived at,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">came to,</hi> (S, Msb, K,) <hi rend="ital">the place,</hi> (S, K,) and <hi rend="ital">the place of abode:</hi> (Msb:) and (so in the S, but in the K “ or, ”) <hi rend="ital">he was, or became, at the point of reaching it, attaining it,</hi> &amp;c. (S, K.) <foreign lang="ar">فَبَلَغْنَ أَجَلَهُنَ</foreign>, in the Kur [ii. 232], means <hi rend="ital">And they have fully attained,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ended, their term.</hi> (Msb.) But <foreign lang="ar">فَإِذَا بَلَغْنَ أَجَلَهُنَّ</foreign>, in the same [lxv. 2], means <hi rend="ital">And when they are near to attaining,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ending, their term:</hi> (S, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">are at the point of accomplishing their term.</hi> (Msb, TA.) It has the first of the meanings explained above in the phrase, <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغَ أَشُدَّهُ</foreign> [Kur xii. 22 &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">He attained his manly vigour,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">full maturity,</hi> &amp;c.]. (TA.) And in <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغَأَرْبَعِينَ سَنَةً</foreign> [Kur xlvii. 14, <hi rend="ital">He attained </hi>the age of <hi rend="ital">forty years</hi>]. (TA.) And in <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغَ مَعَهُ السَّعْىَ</foreign> [Kur xxxvii. 100, <hi rend="ital">He attained to working with him</hi>]. (TA.) In the Kur [iii. 35], occurs the phrase, <foreign lang="ar">وَقَدْ بَلَغَنِىَ الكِبَرُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">When old age hath come to me,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">overtaken me</hi>]: and in another place [xix. 9], <foreign lang="ar">وَ قَدْ بَلَغْتُ مِنَ الكِبَرِ عُتِيًّا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And I have reached the extreme degree of old age:</hi> so explained in the Expos. of the Jel]: phrases like <foreign lang="ar">أَدْرَكَنِىَ الجَهْدُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أَدْرَكْتُهُ</foreign>. (Er-Rághib, TA.) You say also, <foreign lang="ar">لَزِمَهُ ذٰلِكَ <ref cref="n3222-2" target="بَالِغًا" n="2" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>مَا بَلَغَ</foreign> with the accus. case as a denotative of state; meaning [<hi rend="ital">That clave to him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">adhered to him,</hi> &amp;c.,] <hi rend="ital">rising to its highest degree</hi> or <hi rend="ital">point;</hi> from <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">المَنْزِلَ</foreign>, explained above. (Msb.) [But <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n3222-3" target="بَالِغًا" n="3" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>مَا بَلَغَ</foreign> more frequently means <hi rend="ital">Whatever point, degree, amount, sum, quantity, number,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the like, it may reach, attain, arrive at, come to,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">amount to.</hi>] And   
      <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغَ فُلَانٌ <ref cref="n3222-4" target="مَبْلَغَهُ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n3222-5" target="مَبْلَغَتُهُ" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Such a one reached,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">attained, his utmost point</hi> or <hi rend="ital">scope</hi> or <hi rend="ital">degree</hi>]. (TA.) And   
      <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغَ فِى العِلْمِ <ref cref="n3222-6" target="المَبَالِغَ" n="6" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He attained, in knowledge,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">science, the utmost degrees of proficiency</hi>]. (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">الجَوْدَةِ <ref cref="n3222-7" target="مَبْلَغًا" n="7" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>بَلَغَ فِى</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">It reached a consummate degree in goodness</hi>]. (S, K, * TA.) And <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n3222-8" target="مَبْلَغًا" n="8" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>بَلَغَ مِنَ الجَوْدَةِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He attained a consummate degree of goodliness</hi>]: said of a boy that has attained to puberty. (O, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغَ غَايَتَهُ فِى الطَّلَبِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He did his utmost,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">used his utmost power</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ability, in seeking to attain an object</hi>]. (Msb in art. <foreign lang="ar">جهد</foreign>.) And <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغَ أَقْصَى مَجْهُودِ بَعِيرِهِ فِى السَّيْرِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He exerted the utmost endeavour,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">effort,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">power,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">strength, of his camel, in journeying</hi>]. (S in art. <foreign lang="ar">نكث</foreign>.) And <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغَ جَهْدَ دَابَّتِهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">جَهَدَهَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He jaded, harassed, distressed, fatigued,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">wearied, his beast</hi>]: (K in art. <foreign lang="ar">جهد</foreign>:) and in like manner, <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغَ مَشَقَّتَهُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغَ مِنْهُ المَشَقَّةَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">جَهَدَهُ</foreign> [and <foreign lang="ar">شَقَّ عَلَيْهِ</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">He,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, jaded him, harassed him,</hi> &amp;c.; <hi rend="ital">ditressed him, afflicted him, oppressed him, overpowered him:</hi> thus in each of these instances, as in many similar cases, the verb with the inf. n. that follows is equivalent to the verb of that inf. n.]. (Msb in art. <foreign lang="ar">جهد</foreign>.) [And, elliptically, <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغَ مِنْهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغَ مِنْهُ المشَقَّةَ</foreign> , explained above: and often meaning <hi rend="ital">It took,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">had, an effect upon him; it affected him:</hi> frequently said of wine and the like: and of a saying; as in the Ksh and <pb n="251"/> Bd in iv. 66, where <foreign lang="ar">يَبْلُغُ مِنْهُمْ</foreign> is followed by <foreign lang="ar">وَيُؤَثِرُ فِيهِ</foreign> as an explicative: see also <foreign lang="ar">بَلِيغٌ</foreign>.] And <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغْتَ مِنَّا البُلَغِينَ</foreign>, (S, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">البِلَغِينَ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">كُلَّ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مَبْلَغٍ</foreign>: (K:) see <foreign lang="ar">البُلَغِينَ</foreign> below. And <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغْتُ مِنَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الأَمْرِ المَشَقَّةَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I experienced distress from the affair,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">event</hi>]. It is like <foreign lang="ar">البُرَحِينَ</foreign> [and <foreign lang="ar">البِرَحِينَ</foreign>] and <foreign lang="ar">الأَطْوَرِينَ</foreign>; all meaning <hi rend="ital">calamities, misfortunes,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">disasters:</hi> (A'Obeyd, TA:) and is as though they said <foreign lang="ar">خَطْبٌ بِلَغٌ</foreign> [and <foreign lang="ar">بُلَغٌ</foreign>], meaning <foreign lang="ar">بَلِيغٌ</foreign>, and then formed the pl. thus because they considered calamities [as personified, i. e.,] as rational beings having purpose, or design. (IAth, TA.) It is invariably thus, terminating with <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ن</foreign>: or one may say in the nom. case <foreign lang="ar">البُلَغُونَ</foreign>, and in the accus. and gen. <foreign lang="ar">البُلَغِينَ</foreign>. (O, K. *) You say also, <foreign lang="ar">بَلَغَ بِهِ البِلَغِينَ</foreign> [lit. <hi rend="ital">He caused him to come,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">he brought him, to calamity, misfortune,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">disaster,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to distress,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">affliction</hi>]; meaning <hi rend="ital">he went to the utmost point in reviling him, and annoying him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">molesting him.</hi> (IAar, TA.)    </entryFree>2e:Tbb3,<entryFree id="n3236" key="بَلَاغٌ" type="main">
